            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

								<div class="post-15 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-15">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>0.6 &#8212; Compiling your first program</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on May 28th, 2007</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>Before we can write our first program (which we will do very soon), we need to know two things about development environments.</p>
<p>First, although our programs will be written inside .cpp files, the .cpp files themselves will be added to a <strong>project</strong>.  Some IDEs call projects &#8220;workspaces&#8221;, or &#8220;solutions&#8221;.  The project stores the names of all the code files we want to compile, and also saves various IDE settings.  Every time we reopen the project, it will restore the state of the IDE to where we left off.  When we choose to compile our program, the project tells the compiler and linker which files to compile and link.  It is worth noting that project files for one IDE will not work in another IDE.</p>
<p>Second, there are different kinds of projects.  When you create a new project, you will have to pick a project type.  All of the projects that we will create in this tutorial will be <strong>console</strong> projects.  A console project means that we are going to create programs that can be run from the dos or linux command-line.  By default, console applications have no graphical user interface (GUI) and are compiled into stand-alone executable files.  This is perfect for learning C++, because it keeps the complexity to a minimum.</p>
<p>Traditionally, the first program programmers write in a new language is the infamous <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_world" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-article', 'http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_world', 'hello world program']);" >hello world program</a>, and we aren&#8217;t going to deprive you of that experience!  You&#8217;ll thank us later.  Maybe.</p>
<p><strong>A quick note about examples containing code</strong></p>
<p>Starting with this lesson, you will see many examples of C++ code presented.  Most of these examples will look something like this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d739316452465229463" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">

					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0012 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>If you select the code from these examples with your mouse and then copy/paste it into your IDE, you may also get the line numbers (depending on how you made the selection).  If so, you&#8217;ll need to remove these manually.</p>
<p><strong>If you&#8217;re using the Visual Studio IDE</strong></p>
<p><i>Although the following section was written using Visual Studio 2005, it essentially works the same for all versions of Visual Studio.</i></p>
<p>To create a new project in Visual Studio, go to the File menu, and select New -> Project.  A dialog box will pop up that looks like this:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-Project.png" alt="VC2005 Project Dialog" /></p>
<p>First, make sure &#8220;Visual C++&#8221; is selected on the left side.</p>
<p>Second, underneath &#8220;Visual C++&#8221;, select the <em>Win32 project type</em>, and <em>Win32 Console Application</em> will automatically be selected for you.  In the <em>Name</em> field, you will enter the name of your program.  Type in <code>HelloWorld</code>.  In the Location field, pick a directory that you would like your project to be placed into.  We recommend you place them in a subdirectory off of your C drive, such as <code>C:VC2005Projects</code>.  Click OK, and then Finish.</p>
<p>On the left side, in the Solution Explorer, Visual Studio has created a number of files for you, including stdafx.h, HelloWorld.cpp, and stdafx.cpp.</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-Initial.png" alt="Initial Visual C++ program" /></p>
<p>In the text editor, you will see that VC2005 has already created some code for you.  Select and delete the _tmain function, and then type/copy the following into your compiler:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d739316464462385014" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include "stdafx.h"</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-2"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-3">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-4"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-5"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-6"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello world!"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-7"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316464462385014-8"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>What you end up with should look like this:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-HelloWorld.png" alt="Visual C++ hello world program" /></p>
<p>To compile your program, either press F7 or go to the Build menu and choose &#8220;Build Solution&#8221;.  If all goes well, you should see the following appear in the Output window:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-Success.png" alt="Successful build" /></p>
<p>This means your compile was successful!</p>
<p>To run your compiled program, press ctrl-F5, or go the Debug menu and choose &#8220;Start Without Debugging&#8221;.  You will see the following:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-Run.png" alt="Program run" /></p>
<p>That is the result of your program!</p>
<p><strong>Important note to Visual Studio users</strong>: Visual studio programs should ALWAYS begin with the following line:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73931646d961611941" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931646d961611941-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931646d961611941-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include "stdafx.h"</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Otherwise you will receive a compiler warning, such as <code>c:testtest.cpp(21) : fatal error C1010: unexpected end of file while looking for precompiled header directive</code></p>
<p>Alternately, you can turn off precompiled headers.  However, using precompiled headers will make your program compile much faster, so we recommend leaving them on unless you are developing a cross-platform program.</p>
<p>The example programs we show you throughout the tutorial will not include this line, because it is specific to your compiler.</p>
<p><strong>If you&#8217;re using the Code::Blocks IDE</strong></p>
<p>To create a new project, go to the File menu, and select New Project.  A dialog box will pop up that looks like this:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/CB-Project.png" alt="Code::Blocks Project Dialog" /></p>
<p>Select <em>Console Application</em> and press the <em>Create</em> button.</p>
<p>You will be asked to save your project.  You can save it wherever you wish, though we recommend you save it in a subdirectory off of the C drive, such as <code>C:CBProjects</code>.  Name the project <code>HelloWorld</code>.</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/CB-Save.png" alt="Code::Blocks Save Project Dialog" /></p>
<p>You will see &#8220;Console Application&#8221; under the default workspace:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/CB-Closed.png" alt="Code::Blocks Project Closed" /></p>
<p>Open the tree under &#8220;Console Application&#8221;, open &#8220;Sources&#8221;, and double click on &#8220;main.cpp&#8221;.  You will see that the hello world program has already been written for you!</p>
<p>To build your project, press ctrl-F9, or go to the Build menu and choose &#8220;Build&#8221;.  If all goes well, you should see the following appear in the Build log window:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/CB-Success.png" alt="Successful build" /></p>
<p>This means your compile was successful!</p>
<p>To run your compiled program, press ctrl-F10, or go the Build menu and choose &#8220;Run&#8221;.  You will see something similar to the following:</p>
<p><img src="http://learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section0/VC2005-Run.png" alt="Program run" /></p>
<p>That is the result of your program!</p>
<p><strong>If you&#8217;re using a command-line based compiler</strong></p>
<p>Paste the following into a text file named HelloWorld.cpp:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>From the command line, type:</p>
<p><code>g++ -o HelloWorld HelloWorld.cpp</code></p>
<p>This will compile and link HelloWorld.cpp.  To run it, type:</p>
<p><code>HelloWorld</code> (or possibly <code>./HelloWorld</code> or ), and you will see the output of your program.</p>
<p><strong>If you&#8217;re using other IDEs</strong></p>
<p>You will have to figure out how to do the following on your own:<br />
1) Create a console project<br />
2) Add a .cpp file to the project (if necessary)<br />
3) Paste the following code into the file:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-7">7</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-3"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-4"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-5"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello world!"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-6"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931647d500676423-7"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>4) Compile the project<br />
5) Run the project</p>
<p><strong>If compiling fails (aka. &#8220;Oh god something went wrong!&#8221;)</strong></p>
<p>It&#8217;s okay, take a deep breath.  We can probably fix it. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
<p>First, check to ensure that you&#8217;ve typed the code in correctly, with no typos or misspellings (also, make sure you&#8217;re not including line numbers in your code).  The compiler&#8217;s error message may give you a clue as to where or what the problem is.</p>
<p>Second, check section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/07-a-few-common-cpp-problems/">0.7 -- A few common C++ problems</a>, as many common problems are addressed there.</p>
<p>If that fails, try searching for your error message on Google.  It&#8217;s likely someone else has encountered this before and figured out how to fix it.</p>
<p>If you are using a much older C++ compiler, the compiler may give an error about not understanding how to include iostream.  If this is the case, try the following program instead:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d739316484879727306" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-6">6</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d739316484879727306-7">7</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream.h&gt;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-2">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-3"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-4"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-5"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello world!"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-6"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d739316484879727306-7"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0008 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this case, you should upgrade your compiler to something more compliant with recent standards.</p>
<p><strong>If your program runs but the window closes immediately</strong></p>
<p>This is an issue with some compilers, such as Bloodshed&#8217;s Dev-C++.  We present a solution to this problem in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/07-a-few-common-cpp-problems/">0.7 -- a few common C++ problems</a>.</p>
<p><strong>Conclusion</strong></p>
<p>Congratulations, you made it through the <em>hardest part</em> of this tutorial (installing the IDE and compiling your first program)!</p>
<p>Don&#8217;t worry if you don&#8217;t understand what all the different lines in the Hello World program do.  We&#8217;ll look at and explain each line in detail in the upcoming section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/11-structure-of-a-program/">1.1 -- Structure of a program</a>.</p>

</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931e4f1206294910-7"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931e4f1206294910-9"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line 					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>

		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=5473#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5473", "5473", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>I presume you are talking about the difference between:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73931e272359261801" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931e272359261801-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931e272359261801-1"><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello World!"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0003 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>and</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73931e27d387924583" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931e27d387924583-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931e27d387924583-2">2</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931e27d387924583-1"><span class="crayon-r">using</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">namespace</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931e27d387924583-2"><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello World!"</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>It&#8217;s really just two similar but slightly different ways of doing the same thing.  Both should work on all compilers.</p>
<p>To elucidate slightly, the cout object lives inside a namespace called std.  If you just use the name cout, the compiler doesn&#8217;t know to look inside of the std namespace.  Consequently, you have to tell it to look there.  There are two ways to do this: directly (std::cout), or indirectly (using the using statement, which basically sets up a default namespace that the compiler will look in if it can&#8217;t resolve symbols).  Using std::cout is the safer solution, but can make for ugly code if you&#8217;re doing lots of I/O.  In those cases, the using statement can be a better choice.</p>
<p>BTW: Including iostream inside PRE tags seems to work fine for me:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d73931e285781907952" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d73931e285781907952-1">1</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931e285781907952-1"><span class="crayon-p">#include &lt;iostream&gt;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0002 seconds] -->
<p></p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-4 clearfix" id="comment-251035">
		<div id="div-comment-251035" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-251035">
		January 1, 2015 at 2:00 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=251035#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251035", "251035", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When you use the std:: prefix, you&#8217;re referencing a specific thing, so the odds of something going wrong is very small.</p>
<p>When you use &#8220;using namespace std&#8221;, you&#8217;re telling the compiler to check the std namespace whenever it can&#8217;t resolve a name.  This opens up a small possibility that the compiler could resolve a name to something in the std namespace when you didn&#8217;t intend for it to do so.  This is unlikely, so it&#8217;s generally not worth worrying about.</p>
		</div>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-5556">
		<div id="div-comment-5556" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-5556">
		January 5, 2008 at 10:13 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=5556#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-5556", "5556", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Don&#8217;t worry about the namespace thing right now.  I cover namespaces in a future lesson when you&#8217;re better equipped to understand what a namespace is.</p>
<p>If you put using namespace std outside of main (but not in another function), it affects the entire rest of the file.  If you put it inside a function, it only affects rest of the function.</p>
<p>There&#8217;s really no right or wrong way to do it.  I prefer to do it on a function-by-function basis because it&#8217;s slightly safer, but for simple programs either way is fine.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		February 2, 2008 at 7:55 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=7126#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-7126", "7126", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Jessica'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When using a command line to compile (ms vs c   2008 express ed.),  what does the &#8220;-c&#8221; mean in the following command?  (i.e. cl SomeFile.cpp -c).</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-7139">
		<div id="div-comment-7139" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-7139">
		February 3, 2008 at 2:45 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=7139#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-7139", "7139", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Depends on the compiler.  With g++, -c means &#8220;compile to object files, but don&#8217;t link into an executable file&#8221;.  With Microsoft&#8217;s command line compiler, -c doesn&#8217;t mean anything because cl.exe uses slash commands (/) rather than minus commands (-).</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		<p>Hi Alex,</p>
<p>I use Visual C++ 2008 and when I create a Win32 console application I get an extra file: &#8220;targetver.h&#8221;. This file seems to define the minimum configuration required for my program:</p>
<p>#pragma once</p>
<p>// The following macros define the minimum required platform.  The minimum required platform<br />
// is the earliest version of Windows, Internet Explorer etc. that has the necessary features to run<br />
// your application.  The macros work by enabling all features available on platform versions up to and<br />
// including the version specified.</p>
<p>// Modify the following defines if you have to target a platform prior to the ones specified below.<br />
// Refer to MSDN for the latest info on corresponding values for different platforms.<br />
#ifndef _WIN32_WINNT            // Specifies that the minimum required platform is Windows Vista.<br />
#define _WIN32_WINNT 0x0600     // Change this to the appropriate value to target other versions of Windows.<br />
#endif</p>
<p>But I don&#8217;t have Windows Vista, just XP. So far it runs just fine, but I&#8217;m wondering if I shoudn&#8217;t swith for Visual C++ 2005 right now; or can I keep going like that?</p>
<p>This file &#8220;targetver.h&#8221; is called in &#8220;stdafx.h&#8221;, and if I remove the command, it runs again. But maybe some more advanced features will require this file.</p>
<p>To make it short, I&#8217;m just wondering if I can run C++ 2008 without having Vista.</p>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-25378">
		<div id="div-comment-25378" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-25378">
		August 29, 2008 at 3:04 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=25378#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-25378", "25378", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>If I&#8217;m not mistaken (and someone correct me if I am), the _WIN32_WINNT #define tells Visual Studio which set of Windows header files to compile your programs with.  Visual Studio 2008 defaults to 0x0600 because they assume you will be coding Vista programs.  If you&#8217;re coding programs that you want to run on WinXP, you should probably change this to 0x0501 (0x0502 for XP SP2) as this will ensure you don&#8217;t accidentally use Vista-only functions.</p>
<p>Note that this has nothing to do with whether you can run VS2008 on XP -- you can.  It only has to do with what OS the programs you COMPILE using VS2008 can run on.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->

		October 4, 2008 at 9:13 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=29102#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-29102", "29102", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>The information presented on this site is generally platform agnostic.  Anything that is Windows specific is explicitly noted (or should be -- if it isn&#8217;t, let me know).  If you&#8217;re developing on another platform, the code presented in these tutorials should work (assuming your compiler implements language support correctly), but you will of course have to figure out how to actually get it to compile yourself. <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=44814#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-44814", "44814", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to wert'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>i have found that the first-run compiler autodetection fails on vista. or maybe it is that it never even runs. you need to go into the compiler settings and the toolchain executables tab and choose autodetect. this should find the mingw compiler that should have been installed with your codeblocks (you should be running the codeblocks installer that comes WITH mingw and has mingw in the name, unless you are installing it seperately). this fixed the invalid compiler error for me.</p>
		</div>

		<div id="div-comment-58859" class="clearfix comment-container">

		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/10dc9f8052d5a4b080c620a4467e54f7?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/10dc9f8052d5a4b080c620a4467e54f7?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">csvan</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-58859">
		April 23, 2009 at 2:54 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=58859#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-58859", "58859", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to csvan'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You need to download and install a compiler I think, I do not believe Code::Blocks comes packed with one. A good compiler to use is the GCC (Gnu Compiler Collection), but to my knowledge it can be quite hard to set up a compiler on your own if you do not have the appropriate knowledge.</p>
<p>Depending on what platform you use, there are solutions to this. If you run OSX (as I do), you will find GCC and the complete IDE Xcode on the installation disc for OSX (just insert it and look for optional installs and Xcode tools), that will install GCC as well.</p>
<p>If you are running Windows, I would suggest downloading and using DevC++, its good, and comes with a compiler out of the box I think.</p>
<p>Email me if you have further problems (csvanefalk@hushmail.me)</p>
		</div>

		</div>
		<p>It&#8217;s worth mentioning that Linux distros do not necessarily have xterm installed.  CodeBlocks can be modified to use the gnometerminal through Settings &gt; Environment and change the Terminal to launch program to &#8220;gnome-terminal -x&#8221;.</p>
<p>You don&#8217;t have to install xterm.</p>
<p>john</p>

		<p>First, you have the word &#8220;count&#8221; instead of &#8220;cout&#8221;.<br />
Second, after &#8220;int main()&#8221;, you must start the line out with a curly brace { and end it with a curly brace }.<br />
You&#8217;re using an open parentheses ( and a close parentheses ).</p>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251036">
		<div id="div-comment-251036" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-251036">
		January 1, 2015 at 2:10 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=251036#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251036", "251036", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Start without debugging means just run your program like normal.</p>
<p>Start with debugging means run your program with the debugger active, so you can try and figure out what&#8217;s wrong with your program.</p>
<p>For now, run your program without debugging.  I cover debugging in more detail in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/a4-debugging-your-program-stepping-and-breakpoints/" rel="nofollow">A.4 -- Debugging your program (stepping and breakpoints)</a></p>
		</div>

		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cb2642db6bc29b6454694dd37456c027?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/cb2642db6bc29b6454694dd37456c027?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Sid</span>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-78487">
		February 17, 2010 at 2:30 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=78487#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-78487", "78487", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Sid'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Hey, for those using XCode I figured it out.</p>
<p>1. Open XCode.<br />
2. File/New Project&#8230;<br />
3. In the &#8220;New Project&#8221; Assistant, click on &#8220;Command Line Tool&#8221;.<br />
4. Below select &#8220;C++ Tool&#8221; as Type<br />
5. Click &#8220;Next&#8221;<br />
6. Give a project name and directory, then click &#8220;Finish&#8221;.<br />
7. Press Cmd-Shift-R to open the Console window. Output will appear there.<br />
8. Click the &#8220;Build and Go&#8221; toolbar button.</p>
		</div>

<p>Personally I couldn&#8217;t find the &#8220;Start Without Debugging&#8221; option, so I just used CTRL+F5 and it worked fine.</p>

				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-177769">
		September 9, 2014 at 9:10 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=177769#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-177769", "177769", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Brian64'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>fix for issue:</p>
<p>1&gt; Build started: Project: helloWorld2, Configuration: Debug Win32 <br />
1&gt;LINK : fatal error LNK1123: failure during conversion to COFF: file invalid or corrupt<br />
========== Build: 0 succeeded, 1 failed, 0 up-to-date, 0 skipped ==========</p>
<p>Project Properties<br />
   -&gt; Configuration Properties<br />
       -&gt; Linker (General)<br />
          -&gt; Enable Incremental Linking -&gt; &#8220;No (/INCREMENTAL:NO)&#8221;</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">

		<p>ok for anybody using visualstudio 2010 and getting this error:<br />
1&gt;LINK : fatal error LNK1123: failure during conversion to COFF: file invalid or corrupt<br />
you need to do this:<br />
go to project properties under tthe project menu<br />
then go to configuration properties/linker/general<br />
once there change enable incremental linking to no<br />
hope this helps</p>

						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-1"><span class="crayon-c">// Hello World.cpp : Defines the entry point for the console application.</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-2"><span class="crayon-c">//</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-3">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-4"><span class="crayon-p">#include "stdafx.h"</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-5"><span class="crayon-p">#include </span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-6">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-7"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-8"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-9"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-s">"Hello World!"</span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-v">std</span><span class="crayon-o">::</span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d73931b6cb549846833-10"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>

		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0fbac3440004ca15cee139dd77c8da2c?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/0fbac3440004ca15cee139dd77c8da2c?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Akshit S</span>

		</div>
		<p>like you said that we use iostream header file to make use of I/O functionality such as cout. Then why do we need to include &quot;using namespace std&quot; when the compiler is already aware of the existence of cout object in iostream header file?</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-251683">
		<div id="div-comment-251683" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-251683">
		March 1, 2015 at 6:17 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=251683#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-251683", "251683", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>When you #include <iostream>, it pulls all the declarations from the iostream header into your program.  However, it&#8217;s up to you to access them properly.</p>
<p>All of the functionality in iostream (and in all the C++ standard library headers) lives in a namespace called std.  The compiler knows that cout lives within the std namespace.  However, if you just write &#8220;cout&#8221; with no std:: prefix or using statement, it won&#8217;t assume you want the one in the std namespace.  You have to explicitly tell it you want the cout that lives in the std namespace.  There are a few different ways to do that, which are discussed further in section <a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/1-3a-a-first-look-at-cout-cin-endl-namespaces-and-using-statements/" rel="nofollow">1.3a -- A first look at cout, cin, endl, namespaces, and using statements</a>.</iostream></p>
		</div>

<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-252282">
		<div id="div-comment-252282" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Alex</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/#comment-252282">
		April 28, 2015 at 1:46 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/06-writing-your-first-program/?replytocom=252282#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-252282", "252282", "respond", "15" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>If you&#8217;ve changed your project since pressing ctrl-F5, this is normal -- Visual Studio is telling you that it needs to rebuild the project.  However, if you haven&#8217;t changed anything since your last run and you&#8217;re still getting this every time, then something is wrong with your project and/or configuration.</p>
<p>There are some good ideas about how to diagnose this and/or fix this problem on <a href="http://stackoverflow.com/questions/2762930/vs2010-always-thinks-project-is-out-of-date-but-nothing-has-changed" onclick="_gaq.push(['_trackEvent', 'outbound-comment', 'http://stackoverflow.com/questions/2762930/vs2010-always-thinks-project-is-out-of-date-but-nothing-has-changed', 'Stack Overflow']);" rel="nofollow">Stack Overflow</a>.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->
</ul><!-- .children -->
